<p>In the off-season, the team traded outfielder <a href="/wiki/Drew_Stubbs" title="Drew Stubbs">Drew Stubbs</a>, as part of a three team deal with the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>, to the Indians, and in turn received right fielder <a href="/wiki/Shin-Soo_Choo" title="Shin-Soo Choo">Shin-Soo Choo</a>. On July 2, 2013, Homer Bailey pitched a no-hitter against the San Francisco Giants for a 4-0 Reds victory, making Bailey the third pitcher in Reds history with two complete game no-hitters in their career.</p>
<p>Following six consecutive losses to close out the 2013 season, including a loss to the Pittsburgh Pirates, at PNC Park, in the National League wild-card playoff game, the Reds decided to fire Dusty Baker. During his six years as manager, Baker led the Reds to the playoff three times; however, they never advanced beyond the first round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 22, 2013, the Reds hired pitching coach <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Price" title="Bryan Price">Bryan Price</a> to replace Baker as manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Price" title="Bryan Price">Bryan Price</a>, the Reds were led by pitchers <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cueto" title="Johnny Cueto">Johnny Cueto</a> and the hard-throwing Cuban <a href="/wiki/Aroldis_Chapman" title="Aroldis Chapman">Aroldis Chapman</a>. While the offense was led by all-star third baseman <a href="/wiki/Todd_Frazier" title="Todd Frazier">Todd Frazier</a>, Joey Votto, and Brandon Phillips. Although with plenty of star power, the Reds never got off to a good start and ending the season in lowly fourth place in the division to go along with a 76-86 record. During the offseason, the Reds traded pitchers <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Sim%C3%B3n" title="Alfredo Simón">Alfredo Simón</a> to the Tigers and <a href="/wiki/Mat_Latos" title="Mat Latos">Mat Latos</a> to the Marlins. In return, they acquired young talents such as <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Eugenio Suárez">Eugenio Suárez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_DeSclafani" title="Anthony DeSclafani">Anthony DeSclafani</a> They also acquired veteran slugger <a href="/wiki/Marlon_Byrd" title="Marlon Byrd">Marlon Byrd</a> from the Phillies to play left field.</p>
<p>The Reds' 2015 season wasn't much better, as they finished with the second worst record in the league with a record of 64-98, their worst finish since 1982. The Reds were forced to trade star pitchers <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cueto" title="Johnny Cueto">Johnny Cueto</a> (to the Kansas City Royals) and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Leake" title="Mike Leake">Mike Leake</a> (to the San Francisco Giants), receiving minor league pitching prospects for both. Shortly after the season's end, the Reds traded home run derby champion <a href="/wiki/Todd_Frazier" title="Todd Frazier">Todd Frazier</a> to the Chicago White Sox, and closing pitcher <a href="/wiki/Aroldis_Chapman" title="Aroldis Chapman">Aroldis Chapman</a> to the New York Yankees.</p>
<p>In 2016, the Reds broke the record for home runs allowed during a single season. The previous record holder was the 1996 Detroit Tigers with 241 home runs yielded to opposing teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The Reds went 68-94, and again were one of the worst teams in the MLB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The Reds traded outfielder <a href="/wiki/Jay_Bruce" title="Jay Bruce">Jay Bruce</a> to the Mets just before the July 31st non-waiver trade deadline in exchange for two prospects, infielder <a href="/wiki/Dilson_Herrera" title="Dilson Herrera">Dilson Herrera</a> and pitcher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Max_Wotell" title="Max Wotell">Max Wotell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ballpark">Ballpark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ballpark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_American_Ballpark" title="Great American Ballpark">Great American Ballpark</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great-american-ball-park.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Great-american-ball-park.jpg/220px-Great-american-ball-park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Great-american-ball-park.jpg/330px-Great-american-ball-park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Great-american-ball-park.jpg/440px-Great-american-ball-park.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Great-american-ball-park.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Great_American_Ball_Park" title="Great American Ball Park">Great American Ball Park</a> opened in 2003 along the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Cincinnati Reds play their home games at Great American Ball Park, located at 100 Joe Nuxhall Way, in downtown Cincinnati. Great American Ball Park opened in 2003 at the cost of $290 million and has a capacity of 42,271. Along with serving as the home field for the Reds, the stadium also holds the Cincinnati Reds Hall of Fame. The Hall of Fame was added as a part of Reds tradition allowing fans to walk through the history of the franchise as well as participating in many interactive baseball features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Great American Ball Park is the seventh home of the Cincinnati Reds, built immediately to the north of the site on which <a href="/wiki/Riverfront_Stadium" title="Riverfront Stadium">Riverfront Stadium</a>, later named Cinergy Field, once stood. The first ballpark the Reds occupied was <a href="/wiki/Bank_Street_Grounds" title="Bank Street Grounds">Bank Street Grounds</a> from 1882 to 1883 until they moved to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/League_Park_I_(Cincinnati)" title="League Park I (Cincinnati)">League Park I</a> in 1884, where they would remain until 1893. Through the late 1890s and early 1900s (decade), the Reds moved to two different parks where they stayed for less than ten years. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/League_Park_II_(Cincinnati)" title="League Park II (Cincinnati)">League Park II</a> was the third home field for the Reds from 1894 to 1901, and then moved to the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Fans" title="Palace of the Fans">Palace of the Fans</a> which served as the home of the Reds in the 1910s. It was in 1912 that the Reds moved to <a href="/wiki/Crosley_Field" title="Crosley Field">Crosley Field</a> which they called home for fifty-eight years. Crosley served as the home field for the Reds for two <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> titles and five <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> pennants. Beginning June 30, 1970, and during the dynasty of the Big Red Machine, the Reds played in <a href="/wiki/Riverfront_Stadium" title="Riverfront Stadium">Riverfront Stadium</a>, appropriately named due to its location right by the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>. Riverfront saw three World Series titles and five National League pennants. It was in the late 1990s that the city agreed to build two separate stadiums on the riverfront for the Reds and the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a>. Thus, in 2003, the Reds began a new era with the opening of the current stadium.</p>
<p>The Reds hold their spring training in <a href="/wiki/Goodyear,_Arizona" title="Goodyear, Arizona">Goodyear, Arizona</a> at <a href="/wiki/Goodyear_Ballpark" title="Goodyear Ballpark">Goodyear Ballpark</a>. The Reds moved into this stadium and the Cactus League in 2010 after staying in the Grapefruit League for most of their history. The Reds share Goodyear Park with their rivals in <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_uniforms">Logos and uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Logos and uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Logos_and_uniforms_of_the_Cincinnati_Reds" title="Logos and uniforms of the Cincinnati Reds">Logos and uniforms of the Cincinnati Reds</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:328px;max-width:328px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reds_3.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="239" data-file-width="325" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9f/Reds_3.png/160px-Reds_3.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9f/Reds_3.png/240px-Reds_3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9f/Reds_3.png/320px-Reds_3.png 2x" width="160"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Logo of the Reds during the "Big Red Machine"</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NLC-CIN-Logo.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="325" data-file-width="325" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/NLC-CIN-Logo.png/160px-NLC-CIN-Logo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/NLC-CIN-Logo.png/240px-NLC-CIN-Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/NLC-CIN-Logo.png/320px-NLC-CIN-Logo.png 2x" width="160"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Current logo of the Reds</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout the history of the Cincinnati Reds, many different variations of the classic wishbone "C" logo have been introduced. For most of the history of the Reds, especially during the early history, the Reds logo has been simply the wishbone "C" with the word "REDS" inside, the only colors used being red and white. However, during the 1950s, during the renaming and re-branding of the team as the Cincinnati Redlegs because of the connections to communism of the word 'Reds', the color blue was introduced as part of the Reds color combination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> During the 1960s and 1970s the Reds saw a move towards the more traditional colors, abandoning the navy blue. A new logo also appeared with the new era of baseball in 1972, when the team went away from the script "REDS" inside of the "C", instead, putting their mascot Mr. Redlegs in its place as well as putting the name of the team inside of the wishbone "C". In the 1990s the more traditional, early logos of Reds came back with the current logo reflecting more of what the team's logo was when they were first founded.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniform">Uniform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Uniform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:164px;max-width:164px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scott_Rolen_on_June_25,_2011.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2248" data-file-width="1405" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Scott_Rolen_on_June_25%2C_2011.jpg/160px-Scott_Rolen_on_June_25%2C_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Scott_Rolen_on_June_25%2C_2011.jpg/240px-Scott_Rolen_on_June_25%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Scott_Rolen_on_June_25%2C_2011.jpg/320px-Scott_Rolen_on_June_25%2C_2011.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Scott_Rolen" title="Scott Rolen">Scott Rolen</a> wearing the current Reds away uniform, featuring classic lettering.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Along with the logo, the Reds' uniforms have been changed many different times throughout their history. Following their departure from being called the "Redlegs" in 1956 the Reds made a groundbreaking change to their uniforms with the use of sleeveless jerseys, seen only once before in the Major Leagues by the Chicago Cubs. At home and away, the cap was all-red with a white wishbone C insignia. The long-sleeved undershirts were red. The uniform was plain white with a red wishbone C logo on the left and the uniform number on the right. On the road the wishbone C was replaced by the mustachioed "Mr. Red" logo, the pillbox-hat-wearing man with a baseball for a head. The home stockings were red with six white stripes. The away stockings had only three white stripes.</p>
<p>The Reds changed uniforms again in 1961, when they replaced the traditional wishbone C insignia with an oval C logo, but continued to use the sleeveless jerseys. At home, the Reds wore white caps with the red bill with the oval C in red, white sleeveless jerseys with red pinstripes, with the oval C-REDS logo in black with red lettering on the left breast and the number in red on the right. The gray away uniform included a gray cap with the red oval C and a red bill. Their gray away uniforms, which also included a sleeveless jersey, bore CINCINNATI in an arched block style across with the number below on the left. In 1964, players' last names were placed on the back of each set of uniforms, below the numbers. Those uniforms were scrapped after the 1966 season.</p>
<p>However, the Cincinnati uniform design most familiar to baseball enthusiasts is the one whose basic form, with minor variations, held sway for the 26 seasons from 1967 to 1992. Most significantly, the point was restored to the C insignia, making it a wishbone again. During this era, the Reds wore all-red caps both at home and on the road. The caps bore the simple wishbone C insignia in white. The uniforms were standard short-sleeved jerseys and standard trousers—white at home and grey on the road. The home uniform featured the Wishbone C-REDS logo in red with white type on the left breast and the uniform number in red on the right. The away uniform bore CINCINNATI in an arched block style across the front with the uniform number below on the left. Red, long-sleeved undershirts and plain red stirrups over white sanitary stockings completed the basic design.</p>
<p>The 1993 uniforms (which did away with the pullovers and brought back button-down jerseys) kept white and gray as the base colors for the home and away uniforms, but added red pinstripes. The home jerseys were sleeveless, showing more of the red undershirts. The color scheme of the C-REDS logo on the home uniform was reversed, now red lettering on a white background. A new home cap was created that had a red bill and a white crown with red pinstripes and a red wishbone C insignia. The away uniform kept the all-red cap, but moved the uniform number to the left, to more closely match the home uniform. The only additional change to these uniforms was the introduction of black as a primary color of the Reds in 1999, especially on their road uniforms.</p>
<p>The Reds latest uniform change came in December 2006 which differed significantly from the uniforms worn during the previous eight seasons. The home caps returned to an all-red design with a white wishbone C, lightly outlined in black. Caps with red crowns and a black bill became the new road caps. Additionally, the sleeveless jersey was abandoned for a more traditional design. The numbers and lettering for the names on the backs of the jerseys were changed to an early-1900s style typeface, and a handlebar mustached "Mr. Redlegs" – reminiscent of the logo used by the Reds in the 1950s and 1960s – was placed on the left sleeve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards and accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Awards and accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">List of Major League Baseball retired numbers</a></div>
<p>The Cincinnati Reds have retired ten numbers in franchise history, as well as honoring <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>, retired in all major league baseball.</p>
<p>All of the retired numbers are located at Great American Ball Park behind home-plate on the outside of the press box. Along with the retired player and manager number, the following broadcasters are honored with microphones by the broadcast booth: <a href="/wiki/Marty_Brennaman" title="Marty Brennaman">Marty Brennaman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waite_Hoyt" title="Waite Hoyt">Waite Hoyt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Nuxhall" title="Joe Nuxhall">Joe Nuxhall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>

<p>On April 15, 1997, #42 was retired throughout Major League Baseball in honor of <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ohio_Cup">Ohio Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ohio Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Cup" title="Ohio Cup">Ohio Cup</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="1900" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg/175px-Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg/263px-Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg/350px-Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Cup" title="Ohio Cup">Ohio Cup</a> trophy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Ohio Cup was an annual <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">pre-season</a> <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> game, which pitted the <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> rivals <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> and Cincinnati Reds. In its first series it was a single-game cup, played each year at minor-league <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Stadium" title="Cooper Stadium">Cooper Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>, was staged just days before the start of each new <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> season.</p>
<p>A total of eight Ohio Cup games were played, in 1989 to 1996, with the Indians winning six of them. The winner of the game each year was awarded the Ohio Cup in postgame ceremonies. The Ohio Cup was a favorite among baseball fans in Columbus, with attendances regularly topping 15,000.</p>
<p>The Ohio Cup games ended with the introduction of regular-season <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague play</a> in 1997. Thereafter, the two teams competed annually in the regular-season Battle of Ohio or Buckeye Series. The Ohio Cup was revived in 2008 as a reward for the team with the better overall record in the Reds-Indians series each year.</p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marty_Brennaman.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1716" data-file-width="1205" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Marty_Brennaman.jpg/150px-Marty_Brennaman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Marty_Brennaman.jpg/225px-Marty_Brennaman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Marty_Brennaman.jpg/300px-Marty_Brennaman.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marty_Brennaman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Marty Brennaman, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> "voice of the Reds"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Reds' <a href="/wiki/Flagship_(broadcasting)" title="Flagship (broadcasting)">flagship</a> <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">radio station</a> has been <a href="/wiki/WLW" title="WLW">WLW</a>, 700AM since 1969. Prior to that, the Reds were heard over: WKRC, WCPO, WSAI and WCKY. WLW, a 50,000-watt station, is "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clear-channel_stations" title="Clear-channel stations">clear channel</a>" in more than one way, as <a href="/wiki/IHeartMedia" title="IHeartMedia">iHeartMedia</a> owns the "blowtorch" outlet which is also known as "The Nation's Station".</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Marty_Brennaman" title="Marty Brennaman">Marty Brennaman</a> has been the Reds' play-by-play voice since 1974 and has won the <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a> for his work, which includes his famous call of "... and this one belongs to the Reds!" after a win. Joining him for years on color was former Reds pitcher <a href="/wiki/Joe_Nuxhall" title="Joe Nuxhall">Joe Nuxhall</a>, who worked in the radio booth from 1967 (the year after his retirement as an active player) until 2004, plus three more seasons doing select home games until his death, in 2007.</p>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Thom_Brennaman" title="Thom Brennaman">Thom Brennaman</a>, a veteran announcer seen nationwide on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(USA)" title="Fox Sports (USA)">Fox Sports</a>, joined his father <a href="/wiki/Marty_Brennaman" title="Marty Brennaman">Marty</a> in the radio booth. Retired relief pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Brantley" title="Jeff Brantley">Jeff Brantley</a>, formerly of ESPN, also joined the network in 2007. As of 2010, Brantley and Thom Brennaman's increased TV schedule (see below) has led to more appearances for Jim Kelch, who had filled in on the network since 2008.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(July 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Televised games are seen exclusively on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Ohio" title="Fox Sports Ohio">Fox Sports Ohio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Indiana" title="Fox Sports Indiana">Fox Sports Indiana</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_South" title="Fox Sports South">Fox Sports South</a> televises Fox Sports Ohio broadcasts of Reds games to Tennessee and western North Carolina. <a href="/wiki/George_Grande" title="George Grande">George Grande</a>, who hosted the first <i><a href="/wiki/SportsCenter" title="SportsCenter">SportsCenter</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> in 1979, was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Play-by-play" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> announcer, usually alongside <a href="/wiki/Chris_Welsh" title="Chris Welsh">Chris Welsh</a>, from 1993 until his retirement during the final game of the 2009 season. Since 2009, Grande has worked part-time for the Reds as play-by-play announcer in September when Thom Brennaman is covering the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> for <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports" title="Fox Sports">Fox Sports</a>. He has also made guest appearances throughout the season. Brennaman has been the head play-by-play commentator since 2010, with Welsh and Brantley sharing time as the color commentators. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Keels" title="Paul Keels">Paul Keels</a>, who left in 2011 to become the play-by-play announcer for the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes" title="Ohio State Buckeyes">Ohio State Buckeyes</a> Radio Network, was the Reds backup play-by-play television announcer during the 2010 season. Jim Kelch served as Keels' replacement. The Reds also added former Cincinnati First Baseman <a href="/wiki/Sean_Casey_(baseball)" title="Sean Casey (baseball)">Sean Casey</a> – known as "The Mayor" by Reds fans – to do color commentary for approximately 15 games in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WLWT" title="WLWT">WLWT</a> carried Reds games from 1948 to 1995. Among those that have called games for WLWT include <a href="/wiki/Waite_Hoyt" title="Waite Hoyt">Waite Hoyt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ray_Lane_(sportsman)" title="Ray Lane (sportsman)">Ray Lane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Physioc" title="Steve Physioc">Steve Physioc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Bench" title="Johnny Bench">Johnny Bench</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Morgan" title="Joe Morgan">Joe Morgan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Wilson_(sportscaster)" title="Ken Wilson (sportscaster)">Ken Wilson</a>. <a href="/wiki/Al_Michaels" title="Al Michaels">Al Michaels</a>, who established a long career with ABC and NBC, spent three years in Cincinnati early in his career. The last regularly-scheduled, over-the-air broadcasts of Reds games were on <a href="/wiki/WSTR-TV" title="WSTR-TV">WSTR-TV</a> from 1996 to 1998. Since 2010, <a href="/wiki/WKRC-TV" title="WKRC-TV">WKRC-TV</a> has <a href="/wiki/Simulcast" title="Simulcast">simulcast</a> Opening Day games with Fox Sports Ohio.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_league_affiliations">Minor league affiliations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cincinnati_Reds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Minor league affiliations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable">
